## Section 001: Kotlin Spring Ktor Idioms
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Kotlin Spring Ktor Idioms", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title identifies Spring and Ktor but does not yet define the framework-choice, execution-model, and boundary decisions that this operational reference owns
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Kotlin Spring Ktor Idioms", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because framework continuity preserves tested lifecycle behavior and team conventions, while an explicit execution-path trace exposes blocking, transaction, serialization, and error-mapping hazards before code is changed
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Kotlin Spring Ktor Idioms", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the task is actually a framework migration, the repository mixes servlet, reactive, and coroutine models without an owned boundary, or production constraints are unknown and generic idioms would disguise architectural risk
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Kotlin Spring Ktor Idioms", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this reference after the service boundary and active framework are discoverable; do not use it to choose an entire platform without workload, team, migration, and operations evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Kotlin Spring Ktor Idioms", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add an opening operating contract that classifies Spring, Ktor, and shared Kotlin decisions, names the execution-path trace, defines migration and mixed-model stop conditions, and requires repository-backed verification
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Kotlin Spring Ktor Idioms", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that framework idioms are dependency-topology decisions rather than formatting preferences; a locally elegant handler can still be unsafe when its scheduler, transaction, serializer, or lifecycle assumptions conflict with the surrounding stack

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Kotlin Spring Ktor Idioms", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: the task is actually a framework migration, the repository mixes servlet, reactive, and coroutine models without an owned boundary, or production constraints are unknown and generic idioms would disguise architectural risk
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Kotlin Spring Ktor Idioms", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are treating Spring and Ktor as interchangeable syntax, adding suspend functions over blocking JDBC, using Kotlin data classes blindly for JPA entities, relying on global mutable Ktor services, scattering response mapping, and claiming performance from framework reputation rather than measurements
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Kotlin Spring Ktor Idioms", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where the service boundary is known, build files reveal the active framework and plugins, request handlers delegate to application services, and tests can exercise the real serialization and persistence edges

## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed table correctly distinguishes one local corpus file from four public sources, but its broad usage roles do not yet say which concrete Spring, Ktor, coroutine, or Kotlin claim each row may support
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because assigning a narrow evidentiary role to each row prevents a credible source in one domain from being stretched into authority over another, such as using a tutorial to prove scheduler behavior or a local note to assert current API compatibility
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a row is treated as blanket approval for a framework, a public URL is assumed fresh without inspection, the local corpus is mistaken for repository code, or cross-framework advice is synthesized without recording which facts came from which source
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use the table to route and label evidence for this theme, not to replace direct inspection of a target repository or to certify current public APIs
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add a claim-to-source routing protocol, explicit disallowed evidence joins, repository corroboration requirements, and a compact audit record for each version-sensitive recommendation
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that a source map is useful only when it constrains claim propagation; the map should make unsupported joins visible, not merely make the reference look researched

## Section 004: Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed thesis says to load the local corpus, check public guidance, and produce verification-backed decisions, but it does not explain how Spring and Ktor execution models alter that synthesis
- **supporting_reason:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Kotlin syntax can make Spring and Ktor code look similarly concise while their proxying, plugin lifecycle, threading, transaction, serialization, and test harness assumptions remain materially different
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: idiomatic language features are used to erase framework lifecycle requirements, public examples replace target-repository evidence, or verification checks only syntax while missing scheduler, proxy, transaction, or serialization behavior
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply the thesis to framework-specific implementation and review after the service boundary is clear, not to organization-wide platform selection or unmeasured migration claims
- **revision_decision:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace the generic synthesis with an alignment thesis, enumerate the hidden framework semantics, require a lifecycle trace, and retain explicit mixed-model and unknown-workload stop conditions
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the shared Kotlin language is the least decisive layer in many backend choices; lifecycle and dependency semantics dominate once code enters a framework-managed request

- **current_section_observation:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to treat idiomatic Kotlin backend design as alignment among the repository's selected framework, its actual blocking or non-blocking dependencies, stable transport and domain boundaries, and a testable operational contract

## Section 007: Anti Pattern Registry Table

- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed registry catches generic sourcing failures but omits framework-native hazards such as proxy mismatch, blocking reactive paths, transaction leakage, serializer drift, and lifecycle-heavy Kotlin types
- **supporting_reason:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because source discipline prevents unsupported advice, while framework-specific detection prevents well-sourced guidance from being misapplied to a repository with incompatible lifecycle or dependency behavior
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the registry becomes a generic checklist detached from the changed path, every variation is labeled an anti-pattern, or a detected safety issue is waived because the source recommendation is otherwise idiomatic
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply only rows implicated by the task's framework and changed path; do not use the registry to force stylistic uniformity or redesign unrelated modules
- **revision_decision:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to extend the registry concept with framework-native signals, false-positive boundaries, evidence fields, and recovery choices while preserving the original three provenance rows

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed provides one archive-wide generation verifier command, but it does not distinguish document-structure validation from framework behavior, repository build, request-path, or operational verification
- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a document verifier proves structural contracts, whereas only repository-specific execution can reveal proxying, dispatcher, transaction, plugin, serializer, and lifecycle mistakes
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the archive command is assumed to exist in another repository, a green Markdown verifier is reported as runtime proof, broad test success hides an unexercised path, or flaky infrastructure is retried without classification
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use the document commands for this corpus and select target tests from the owning repository; do not invent universal Gradle tasks or production SLO proof
- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to define structural, build, transport, integration, and operational layers; preserve the original command; add evidence-capture fields and prohibit scope inflation
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that verification is a ladder of claims: each rung may prove only its own scope, and evidence becomes misleading when a lower-cost structural check is promoted into proof of a higher-risk runtime property

### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed offers adopt, adapt, avoid, and cost-of-error rows at the theme level, but it does not compare the principal Spring, Ktor, blocking, reactive, coroutine, and interop choices
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the smallest reliable choice usually preserves proven boundaries, while adaptation localizes unavoidable mismatch and avoidance prevents convenience syntax from hiding systemic incompatibility
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: adoption perpetuates an unsafe legacy path, adaptation leaks across layers, avoidance is based only on preference, or the cost-of-error row is acknowledged without changing rollout or verification depth
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply the guide to a bounded service or capability decision with known dependencies; use a dedicated architecture process for platform replacement
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add option-specific conditions and consequences, require a graph-displacement and rollback comparison, and make cost-of-error determine verification and rollout depth
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that adopt, adapt, and avoid are topology choices: they describe how much of the dependency and lifecycle graph must change, so review depth should scale with graph displacement rather than code-line count
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to adopt repository-native conventions when framework and dependencies align; adapt at explicit adapters when one blocking, Java-interop, serializer, or persistence edge differs; avoid combining models that cannot preserve scheduler, transaction, or lifecycle safety; and escalate migrations or production-critical changes with unclear rollback
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the smallest reliable choice usually preserves proven boundaries, while adaptation localizes unavoidable mismatch and avoidance prevents convenience syntax from hiding systemic incompatibility
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; adoption perpetuates an unsafe legacy path, adaptation leaks across layers, avoidance is based only on preference, or the cost-of-error row is acknowledged without changing rollout or verification depth
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: apply the guide to a bounded service or capability decision with known dependencies; use a dedicated architecture process for platform replacement
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add option-specific conditions and consequences, require a graph-displacement and rollback comparison, and make cost-of-error determine verification and rollout depth
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies adopt, adapt, and avoid are topology choices: they describe how much of the dependency and lifecycle graph must change, so review depth should scale with graph displacement rather than code-line count

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: adoption perpetuates an unsafe legacy path, adaptation leaks across layers, avoidance is based only on preference, or the cost-of-error row is acknowledged without changing rollout or verification depth

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 10 on second-order deductions: its reach is limited where adoption perpetuates an unsafe legacy path, adaptation leaks across layers, avoidance is based only on preference, or the cost-of-error row is acknowledged without changing rollout or verification depth

- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 10 on second-order deductions: change the guidance by applying this concrete revision: add option-specific conditions and consequences, require a graph-displacement and rollback comparison, and make cost-of-error determine verification and rollout depth

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed frames the reference as a service operating aid and proposes one service, 25 endpoints or workers, 1000 representative requests, and one rollback path, but those values are uncalibrated planning bounds
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because coherent ownership and lifecycle boundaries matter more than raw endpoint count, and a bounded batch allows evidence, tests, and rollback to stay causally connected
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the batch spans independent services or teams, endpoint count hides heterogeneous hot paths, 1000 requests do not represent concurrency or tail behavior, rollback requires data repair, or event-loop and blocking workloads are mixed without separate models
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this workload model for review decomposition and representative local verification, not for production capacity certification
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to reinterpret numerical bounds as warning thresholds, center coherent ownership and rollback, add concurrency and side-effect dimensions, and require splitting when causal graphs diverge
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the right unit of scale is the reversible causal graph: a larger endpoint count may be safe when dependencies and rollback are shared, while one endpoint may be too large when it crosses systems and irreversible side effects
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to scope one review batch to a single owned service capability with a traceable request or worker lifecycle, a bounded endpoint set, known persistence and remote dependencies, representative success and failure traffic, and one independently executable rollback; treat the seed numbers as split prompts rather than capacity guarantees
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because coherent ownership and lifecycle boundaries matter more than raw endpoint count, and a bounded batch allows evidence, tests, and rollback to stay causally connected
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; the batch spans independent services or teams, endpoint count hides heterogeneous hot paths, 1000 requests do not represent concurrency or tail behavior, rollback requires data repair, or event-loop and blocking workloads are mixed without separate models
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: use this workload model for review decomposition and representative local verification, not for production capacity certification
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: reinterpret numerical bounds as warning thresholds, center coherent ownership and rollback, add concurrency and side-effect dimensions, and require splitting when causal graphs diverge
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the right unit of scale is the reversible causal graph: a larger endpoint count may be safe when dependencies and rollback are shared, while one endpoint may be too large when it crosses systems and irreversible side effects

### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: 18-of-20 is treated as universal acceptance, two dangerous misses are averaged away, source labels exist without faithful claims, or runtime tests are omitted because the document targets passed

## Section 020: Failure Mode Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed covers evidence drift, generic advice, request surges, and security boundaries, but its triggers and mitigations remain broad and omit framework-specific detection and recovery sequencing
- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a failure table becomes actionable only when an operator or reviewer can distinguish the cause class and choose a bounded response instead of repeating generic tests
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: several causes share a vague timeout label, retries hide saturation, security failures are reduced to input shape, framework exceptions leak to clients, or mitigation changes the execution model without capacity evidence
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this table for design review and controlled verification; follow the service's incident and security procedures during live failures
- **revision_decision:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to expand broad modes into diagnosable framework classes, add owner and containment fields conceptually, and require recovery proof against the original trigger
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that failure modes should be mutually distinguishable enough to prevent harmful recovery overlap; a retry policy, rollback, or dispatcher change is safe only after the cause class is narrowed
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to classify failures across evidence freshness, framework lifecycle, execution-model mismatch, configuration and startup, validation and authorization, transaction and persistence, serialization and error contracts, dependency saturation, cancellation, and rollback; assign each an owner, detector, immediate containment, root-cause gate, and recovery proof

- **revision_decision:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: expand broad modes into diagnosable framework classes, add owner and containment fields conceptually, and require recovery proof against the original trigger

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed distinguishes transient evidence failures and advises bounded retries plus workflow backpressure, but it does not separate document-generation retries from request, client, database, or rollout retries
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because retries multiply work and can convert a local transient failure into system-wide saturation, duplicate side effects, stale transactions, or an agent loop that obscures missing evidence
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: authentication or validation errors are retried, a transaction spans backoff, blocking work ignores cancellation, retry ownership is duplicated across framework and client layers, or source contradictions are treated as temporary
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply conceptual safeguards here, but implement retry mechanics through the target repository's established libraries and service-level policy
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to separate evidence and runtime retries, add idempotency, cancellation, deadline, nested-retry, and shared-budget rules, and define explicit stop-admission signals
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that retry and backpressure are one control loop: retry consumes capacity while backpressure protects it, so they must share a budget and cannot be configured independently by separate layers
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to classify the failing layer first; allow one bounded evidence-refresh retry as the seed states, retry runtime operations only when the failure is transient and the operation is safe or idempotent, honor coroutine cancellation and deadlines, bound attempts and concurrency, and stop admission or rollout when downstream capacity or verification is red
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because retries multiply work and can convert a local transient failure into system-wide saturation, duplicate side effects, stale transactions, or an agent loop that obscures missing evidence
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; authentication or validation errors are retried, a transaction spans backoff, blocking work ignores cancellation, retry ownership is duplicated across framework and client layers, or source contradictions are treated as temporary
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: apply conceptual safeguards here, but implement retry mechanics through the target repository's established libraries and service-level policy
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: separate evidence and runtime retries, add idempotency, cancellation, deadline, nested-retry, and shared-budget rules, and define explicit stop-admission signals
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies retry and backpressure are one control loop: retry consumes capacity while backpressure protects it, so they must share a budget and cannot be configured independently by separate layers
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: the operation has a clear deadline and retry budget, transient errors are distinguishable, side effects are idempotent or deduplicated, downstream capacity is observed, and cancellation reaches the work
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because retries multiply work and can convert a local transient failure into system-wide saturation, duplicate side effects, stale transactions, or an agent loop that obscures missing evidence
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the success case ends where authentication or validation errors are retried, a transaction spans backoff, blocking work ignores cancellation, retry ownership is duplicated across framework and client layers, or source contradictions are treated as temporary

- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: show the second-order benefit that retry and backpressure are one control loop: retry consumes capacity while backpressure protects it, so they must share a budget and cannot be configured independently by separate layers
### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: authentication or validation errors are retried, a transaction spans backoff, blocking work ignores cancellation, retry ownership is duplicated across framework and client layers, or source contradictions are treated as temporary
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are nested Spring and client retries, Ktor request retries around non-idempotent writes, unbounded coroutine launch, retry-after values ignored, jitterless synchronized recovery, swallowed cancellation exceptions, and agent regeneration loops without new evidence
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where the operation has a clear deadline and retry budget, transient errors are distinguishable, side effects are idempotent or deduplicated, downstream capacity is observed, and cancellation reaches the work
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: distinguish a genuine failure from an out-of-scope case using apply conceptual safeguards here, but implement retry mechanics through the target repository's established libraries and service-level policy
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: fail fast with a stable response, queue work with bounded capacity, open a circuit, shed load, use explicit human escalation, refresh one stale source, or roll back the change that introduced saturation
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: retain uncertainty explicitly: framework retry facilities, client semantics, idempotency stores, queue capacities, and production thresholds vary by repository and version
### Question 05: Which alternatives and tradeoffs matter?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: the meaningful alternatives are these: fail fast with a stable response, queue work with bounded capacity, open a circuit, shed load, use explicit human escalation, refresh one stale source, or roll back the change that introduced saturation
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: compare those alternatives against the decision to determine when retry is appropriate, where backpressure must be applied, and how cancellation, idempotency, saturation, and ownership change the choice
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: alternatives become option theater when nested Spring and client retries, Ktor request retries around non-idempotent writes, unbounded coroutine launch, retry-after values ignored, jitterless synchronized recovery, swallowed cancellation exceptions, and agent regeneration loops without new evidence

### Question 06: Which gotchas and failure modes matter most?

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed records source loading, verification proof, latency percentiles, failures, retries, saturation, rollback, and compact audit evidence, but it does not map these signals to Spring or Ktor lifecycle boundaries
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the same user-visible timeout can arise from event-loop blocking, connection-pool exhaustion, remote latency, retry amplification, or transaction contention, so boundary-aware signals are needed to distinguish causes
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: raw request bodies or credentials are logged, exception class names become public contracts, route parameters explode cardinality, averages hide tails, or metrics exist without ownership and thresholds
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: define required semantic signals here, but implement them with the repository's existing telemetry stack and privacy controls
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to map generic signals to request lifecycle boundaries, add cardinality and redaction rules, require failure-path emission tests, and connect every alert to containment or rollback

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed proposes service-specific objectives and fallback p95 under 200 milliseconds plus p99 under 500 milliseconds, yet it does not define workload, environment, concurrency, warmup, or whether those fallback numbers are evidence-based
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because percentile values are meaningful only relative to a workload and environment, and framework execution mistakes often surface first as queue growth or tail latency rather than median slowdown
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the seed's 200/500 values are treated as product objectives, tests run sequentially against fakes, warm caches hide startup or cold behavior, throughput is omitted, or one faster median masks saturation and worse tails
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use the method to design reproducible target-service evidence, not to benchmark Spring against Ktor in the abstract or certify production from local measurements
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain the seed thresholds as visibly provisional, add full workload and environment controls, prioritize baseline deltas and saturation, and prohibit absolute claims without a service-owned objective
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that performance verification tests architecture assumptions: tail growth under concurrency can reveal hidden blocking or unbounded composition even when functional tests and single-request timing remain green
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to use the target service's own objective when available; otherwise establish a documented local baseline and compare representative before-and-after distributions under controlled input, concurrency, warmup, dependency, and resource conditions while reporting throughput, errors, saturation, allocations where relevant, and cancellation behavior
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because percentile values are meaningful only relative to a workload and environment, and framework execution mistakes often surface first as queue growth or tail latency rather than median slowdown
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; the seed's 200/500 values are treated as product objectives, tests run sequentially against fakes, warm caches hide startup or cold behavior, throughput is omitted, or one faster median masks saturation and worse tails

- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: retain the seed thresholds as visibly provisional, add full workload and environment controls, prioritize baseline deltas and saturation, and prohibit absolute claims without a service-owned objective
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies performance verification tests architecture assumptions: tail growth under concurrency can reveal hidden blocking or unbounded composition even when functional tests and single-request timing remain green

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed stops the reference at multiple systems, ownership boundaries, unbounded source discovery, or production traffic without an objective, but it does not describe framework-specific decomposition and reconciliation
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because parallel work is safe only when splits follow genuine ownership and rollback boundaries; splitting by file count can leave transactions, serializers, authentication, and shared DTOs inconsistently governed
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: agents edit the same reference or configuration, Spring and Ktor boundaries share mutable models without an owner, schema rollout spans independent batches, source conclusions conflict silently, or local tests cannot observe cross-service behavior
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this statement to decompose reference-guided work, not as a substitute for distributed-system architecture or organizational design
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add framework and data-coupling split criteria, shared-contract ownership, staged reconciliation, and an end-to-end post-merge gate
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that scale boundaries are coordination boundaries; the decisive question is whether independent work can fail and recover independently while preserving shared contracts
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to split when services have independent ownership or deployment, request paths use materially different execution models or persistence, source discovery cannot be bounded, data changes are not independently reversible, or production rollout lacks service objectives; assign one decision and verification owner per split and reconcile shared contracts explicitly
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because parallel work is safe only when splits follow genuine ownership and rollback boundaries; splitting by file count can leave transactions, serializers, authentication, and shared DTOs inconsistently governed
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; agents edit the same reference or configuration, Spring and Ktor boundaries share mutable models without an owner, schema rollout spans independent batches, source conclusions conflict silently, or local tests cannot observe cross-service behavior
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: use this statement to decompose reference-guided work, not as a substitute for distributed-system architecture or organizational design
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add framework and data-coupling split criteria, shared-contract ownership, staged reconciliation, and an end-to-end post-merge gate

## Section 026: Evidence Boundary Notes
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed defines local, external, and combined inference labels in three bullets, but it does not cover target-repository observations, verification results, conflicts, or confidence changes
- **supporting_reason:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a reader must be able to distinguish what a source says from what the target system demonstrates and from what the author concludes, especially when framework lifecycles and versions differ
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: labels are decorative, an external URL is called evidence without inspection, repository convention is generalized into framework fact, a passing test is stretched beyond its fixture, or conflicting evidence is silently merged
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply the expanded taxonomy to this generated reference and downstream decisions, while retaining the three exact seed labels for compatibility
- **revision_decision:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to preserve the original bullets and add repository observation, executed result, conflict, freshness, applicability, confidence, and falsifier rules plus a final trace audit
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that evidence boundaries are interfaces between knowledge domains; preserving them enables safe substitution when a source changes, while collapsing them creates hidden coupling and expensive re-review
